I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Substrait join consumer produces incorrect logical plan
### Describe the bug

The substrait join consumer produces incorrect logical plan for queries like 
```sql
SELECT t1.id AS t1_id, t2.id AS t2_id, t1.val, t2.val
FROM t1
JOIN t2 ON t1.id = t2.id AND t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val
```

where it assumes the null semantics of one of the join conditions to be the null semantics of the entire join

### To Reproduce

Convert this substrait plan - datafusion/substrait/tests/testdata/test_plans/mixed_join_equal_and_indistinct.json from https://github.com/apache/datafusion/pull/21121/changes

### Expected behavior

If a join with join_keys having mixed null handling i.e. a few join keys with `NullEqNull` and a few with `NullEqNothing` then the resulting outer join should preserve these semantics

### Additional context

_No response_

</pr_description>

    17	
    18	use crate::logical_plan::consumer::SubstraitConsumer;
    19	use datafusion::common::{Column, JoinType, NullEquality, not_impl_err, plan_err};
    20	use datafusion::logical_expr::requalify_sides_if_needed;
    21	use datafusion::logical_expr::utils::split_conjunction;
    22	use datafusion::logical_expr::{
    23	    BinaryExpr, Expr, LogicalPlan, LogicalPlanBuilder, Operator,
    24	};
    25	
    26	use substrait::proto::{JoinRel, join_rel};
    27	
    28	pub async fn from_join_rel(
    29	    consumer: &impl SubstraitConsumer,
    30	    join: &JoinRel,
    31	) -> datafusion::common::Result<LogicalPlan> {
    32	    if join.post_join_filter.is_some() {
    33	        return not_impl_err!("JoinRel with post_join_filter is not yet supported");
    34	    }
    35	
    36	    let left: LogicalPlanBuilder = LogicalPlanBuilder::from(
    37	        consumer.consume_rel(join.left.as_ref().unwrap()).await?,
    38	    );
    39	    let right = LogicalPlanBuilder::from(
    40	        consumer.consume_rel(join.right.as_ref().unwrap()).await?,
    41	    );
    42	    let (left, right, _requalified) = requalify_sides_if_needed(left, right)?;
    43	
    44	    let join_type = from_substrait_jointype(join.r#type)?;
    45	    // The join condition expression needs full input schema and not the output schema from join since we lose columns from
    46	    // certain join types such as semi and anti joins
    47	    let in_join_schema = left.schema().join(right.schema())?;
    48	
    49	    // If join expression exists, parse the `on` condition expression, build join and return
    50	    // Otherwise, build join with only the filter, without join keys
    51	    match &join.expression.as_ref() {
    52	        Some(expr) => {
    53	            let on = consumer.consume_expression(expr, &in_join_schema).await?;
    54	            // The join expression can contain both equal and non-equal ops.
    55	            // As of datafusion 31.0.0, the equal and non equal join conditions are in separate fields.
    56	            // So we extract each part as follows:
    57	            // - If an Eq or IsNotDistinctFrom op is encountered, add the left column, right column and is_null_equal_nulls to `join_ons` vector
    58	            // - Otherwise we add the expression to join_filter (use conjunction if filter already exists)
    59	            let (join_ons, nulls_equal_nulls, join_filter) =
    60	                split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality(&on);
    61	            let (left_cols, right_cols): (Vec<_>, Vec<_>) =
    62	                itertools::multiunzip(join_ons);
    63	            let null_equality = if nulls_equal_nulls {
    64	                NullEquality::NullEqualsNull
    65	            } else {
    66	                NullEquality::NullEqualsNothing
    67	            };
    68	            left.join_detailed(
    69	                right.build()?,
    70	                join_type,
    71	                (left_cols, right_cols),
    72	                join_filter,
    73	                null_equality,
    74	            )?
    75	            .build()
    76	        }
    77	        None => {
    78	            let on: Vec<String> = vec![];
    79	            left.join_detailed(
    80	                right.build()?,
    81	                join_type,
    82	                (on.clone(), on),
    83	                None,
    84	                NullEquality::NullEqualsNothing,
    85	            )?
    86	            .build()
    87	        }
    88	    }
    89	}
    90	
    91	fn split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality(
    92	    filter: &Expr,
    93	) -> (Vec<(Column, Column)>, bool, Option<Expr>) {
    94	    let exprs = split_conjunction(filter);
    95	
    96	    let mut accum_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
    97	    let mut accum_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];
    98	    let mut nulls_equal_nulls = false;
    99	
   100	    for expr in exprs {
   101	        #[expect(clippy::collapsible_match)]
   102	        match expr {
   103	            Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
   104	                x @ (BinaryExpr {
   105	                    left,
   106	                    op: Operator::Eq,
   107	                    right,
   108	                }
   109	                | BinaryExpr {
   110	                    left,
   111	                    op: Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
   112	                    right,
   113	                }) => {
   114	                    nulls_equal_nulls = match x.op {
   115	                        Operator::Eq => false,
   116	                        Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom => true,
   117	                        _ => unreachable!(),
   118	                    };
   119	
   120	                    match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
   121	                        (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
   122	                            accum_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
   123	                        }
   124	                        _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   125	                    }
   126	                }
   127	                _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   128	            },
   129	            _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   130	        }
   131	    }
   132	
   133	    let join_filter = accum_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
   134	    (accum_join_keys, nulls_equal_nulls, join_filter)
   135	}
   136	
   137	fn from_substrait_jointype(join_type: i32) -> datafusion::common::Result<JoinType> {
   138	    if let Ok(substrait_join_type) = join_rel::JoinType::try_from(join_type) {
   139	        match substrait_join_type {
   140	            join_rel::JoinType::Inner => Ok(JoinType::Inner),
   141	            join_rel::JoinType::Left => Ok(JoinType::Left),
   142	            join_rel::JoinType::Right => Ok(JoinType::Right),
   143	            join_rel::JoinType::Outer => Ok(JoinType::Full),
   144	            join_rel::JoinType::LeftAnti => Ok(JoinType::LeftAnti),
   145	            join_rel::JoinType::LeftSemi => Ok(JoinType::LeftSemi),
   146	            join_rel::JoinType::LeftMark => Ok(JoinType::LeftMark),
   147	            join_rel::JoinType::RightMark => Ok(JoinType::RightMark),
   148	            join_rel::JoinType::RightAnti => Ok(JoinType::RightAnti),
   149	            join_rel::JoinType::RightSemi => Ok(JoinType::RightSemi),
   150	            _ => plan_err!("unsupported join type {substrait_join_type:?}"),
   151	        }
   152	    } else {
   153	        plan_err!("invalid join type variant {join_type}")
   154	    }
   155	}
   156

    35	
    36	    async fn tpch_plan_to_string(query_id: i32) -> Result<String> {
    37	        let path =
    38	            format!("tests/testdata/tpch_substrait_plans/query_{query_id:02}_plan.json");
    39	        let proto = serde_json::from_reader::<_, Plan>(BufReader::new(
    40	            File::open(path).expect("file not found"),
    41	        ))
    42	        .expect("failed to parse json");
    43	
    44	        let ctx = add_plan_schemas_to_ctx(SessionContext::new(), &proto)?;
    45	        let plan = from_substrait_plan(&ctx.state(), &proto).await?;
    46	        ctx.state().create_physical_plan(&plan).await?;
    47	        Ok(format!("{plan}"))
    48	    }
    49

Now I understand the issue. The `Join` struct has a single `null_equality` field, which applies to all join keys. But the substrait join consumer needs to handle the case where different join keys have different null semantics.

Looking at the problem more carefully: the current code converts `Eq` and `IsNotDistinctFrom` operators from the substrait plan into a single `null_equality` setting for the entire join. But if you have both types of operators in the same join (e.g., `t1.id = t2.id AND t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val`), only the last one's null semantics is used.

The solution should preserve the original expression semantics. Since DataFusion's `Join` only supports a single `null_equality` per join, the approach should be: when there are mixed null semantics, we can't use join keys for those with `IsNotDistinctFrom` (NullEqualsNull) if the overall join is set to `NullEqualsNothing`. Instead, we should keep the join keys as `Eq` and put the `IsNotDistinctFrom` expressions in the filter.

But wait, let me check what the correct approach should be. Let me look at the producer side too

    18	use crate::logical_plan::producer::{SubstraitProducer, make_binary_op_scalar_func};
    19	use datafusion::common::{
    20	    DFSchemaRef, JoinConstraint, JoinType, NullEquality, not_impl_err,
    21	};
    22	use datafusion::logical_expr::{Expr, Join, Operator};
    23	use std::sync::Arc;
    24	use substrait::proto::rel::RelType;
    25	use substrait::proto::{Expression, JoinRel, Rel, join_rel};
    26	
    27	pub fn from_join(
    28	    producer: &mut impl SubstraitProducer,
    29	    join: &Join,
    30	) -> datafusion::common::Result<Box<Rel>> {
    31	    let left = producer.handle_plan(join.left.as_ref())?;
    32	    let right = producer.handle_plan(join.right.as_ref())?;
    33	    let join_type = to_substrait_jointype(join.join_type);
    34	    // we only support basic joins so return an error for anything not yet supported
    35	    match join.join_constraint {
    36	        JoinConstraint::On => {}
    37	        JoinConstraint::Using => return not_impl_err!("join constraint: `using`"),
    38	    }
    39	    let in_join_schema = Arc::new(join.left.schema().join(join.right.schema())?);
    40	
    41	    // convert filter if present
    42	    let join_filter = match &join.filter {
    43	        Some(filter) => Some(producer.handle_expr(filter, &in_join_schema)?),
    44	        None => None,
    45	    };
    46	
    47	    // map the left and right columns to binary expressions in the form `l = r`
    48	    // build a single expression for the ON condition, such as `l.a = r.a AND l.b = r.b`
    49	    let eq_op = match join.null_equality {
    50	        NullEquality::NullEqualsNothing => Operator::Eq,
    51	        NullEquality::NullEqualsNull => Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
    52	    };
    53	    let join_on = to_substrait_join_expr(producer, &join.on, eq_op, &in_join_schema)?;
    54	
    55	    // create conjunction between `join_on` and `join_filter` to embed all join conditions,
    56	    // whether equal or non-equal in a single expression
    57	    let join_expr = match &join_on {
    58	        Some(on_expr) => match &join_filter {
    59	            Some(filter) => Some(Box::new(make_binary_op_scalar_func(
    60	                producer,
    61	                on_expr,
    62	                filter,
    63	                Operator::And,
    64	            ))),
    65	            None => join_on.map(Box::new), // the join expression will only contain `join_on` if filter doesn't exist
    66	        },
    67	        None => match &join_filter {
    68	            Some(_) => join_filter.map(Box::new), // the join expression will only contain `join_filter` if the `on` condition doesn't exist
    69	            None => None,
    70	        },
    71	    };
    72	
    73	    Ok(Box::new(Rel {
    74	        rel_type: Some(RelType::Join(Box::new(JoinRel {
    75	            common: None,
    76	            left: Some(left),
    77	            right: Some(right),
    78	            r#type: join_type as i32,
    79	            expression: join_expr,
    80	            post_join_filter: None,
    81	            advanced_extension: None,
    82	        }))),
    83	    }))
    84	}
    85	
    86	fn to_substrait_join_expr(
    87	    producer: &mut impl SubstraitProducer,
    88	    join_conditions: &Vec<(Expr, Expr)>,
    89	    eq_op: Operator,
    90	    join_schema: &DFSchemaRef,
    91	) -> datafusion::common::Result<Option<Expression>> {
    92	    // Only support AND conjunction for each binary expression in join conditions
    93	    let mut exprs: Vec<Expression> = vec![];
    94	    for (left, right) in join_conditions {
    95	        let l = producer.handle_expr(left, join_schema)?;
    96	        let r = producer.handle_expr(right, join_schema)?;
    97	        // AND with existing expression
    98	        exprs.push(make_binary_op_scalar_func(producer, &l, &r, eq_op));
    99	    }
   100	
   101	    let join_expr: Option<Expression> =
   102	        exprs.into_iter().reduce(|acc: Expression, e: Expression| {
   103	            make_binary_op_scalar_func(producer, &acc, &e, Operator::And)
   104	        });
   105	    Ok(join_expr)
   106	}
   107	
   108	fn to_substrait_jointype(join_type: JoinType) -> join_rel::JoinType {
   109	    match join_type {
   110	        JoinType::Inner => join_rel::JoinType::Inner,
   111	        JoinType::Left => join_rel::JoinType::Left,
   112	        JoinType::Right => join_rel::JoinType::Right,
   113	        JoinType::Full => join_rel::JoinType::Outer,
   114	        JoinType::LeftAnti => join_rel::JoinType::LeftAnti,
   115	        JoinType::LeftSemi => join_rel::JoinType::LeftSemi,
   116	        JoinType::LeftMark => join_rel::JoinType::LeftMark,
   117	        JoinType::RightMark => join_rel::JoinType::RightMark,
   118	        JoinType::RightAnti => join_rel::JoinType::RightAnti,
   119	        JoinType::RightSemi => join_rel::JoinType::RightSemi,
   120	    }
   121	}

2026-06-01 04:37:34,437 - INFO - swea-agent-apache__datafusion-21121 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I can see the full picture:

1. The **producer** converts ALL join keys to the same operator (all `Eq` or all `IsNotDistinctFrom`) based on the single `null_equality` field.
2. The **consumer** reads the substrait expression and tries to split it into join keys (Eq/IsNotDistinctFrom) and filter. But it uses a single `nulls_equal_nulls` boolean that gets overwritten each iteration.

The problem is that the `Join` struct in DataFusion only supports a single `null_equality` for all join keys. But the substrait plan can have mixed: some keys with `Eq` and some with `IsNotDistinctFrom`.

The key insight from the PR description is: "If a join with join_keys having mixed null handling i.e. a few join keys with `NullEqNull` and a few with `NullEqNothing` then the resulting outer join should preserve these semantics"

There are two possible approaches:
1. When mixed semantics are detected, keep all join keys but use one null_equality, and convert the others to filter expressions.
2. When mixed, put all keys with `IsNotDistinctFrom` (NullEqualsNull) into the filter.

But actually, let me think more carefully. The issue says the current code picks the null semantics of one of the join conditions to be the null semantics of the entire join. That's the bug - `nulls_equal_nulls` is overwritten for each key.

Looking at the code:
- If we have `Eq` keys, `nulls_equal_nulls` should be false
- If we have `IsNotDistinctFrom` keys, `nulls_equal_nulls` should be true
- But if we have both, we can't represent it with a single `null_equality`

The simplest and correct fix: when there are mixed semantics, use `NullEqualsNull` (the more permissive one) for the join keys, but then we'd treat `Eq` keys incorrectly as null-equal. Or we could move the `IsNotDistinctFrom` keys to the filter.

Wait, let me think about this differently. The `NullEquality::NullEqualsNull` means "null == null" (like `IS NOT DISTINCT FROM`), and `NullEquality::NullEqualsNothing` means "null == anything is null" (like regular `=`).

If we have mix of `=` and `IS NOT DISTINCT FROM`, the correct approach would be:
- Keep the `=` keys as join keys with `NullEqualsNothing`
- Move the `IS NOT DISTINCT FROM` to the filter (since we can't have per-key null semantics)

OR:
- Keep both as join keys with `NullEqualsNull` and add filter conditions to exclude nulls for the `=` keys

But actually, the simplest and most correct approach: if all keys have the same null semantics, use that. If mixed, we need to pick one and put the other in the filter.

Actually wait, let me look at this from a different angle. Let me look at what the PR description says more carefully:

> If a join with join_keys having mixed null handling i.e. a few join keys with `NullEqNull` and a few with `NullEqNothing` then the resulting outer join should preserve these semantics

So the expected behavior is to preserve the semantics. But since DataFusion's `Join` only supports a single `null_equality`, we need to handle this differently.

Let me check if there's been any change to make `null_equality` per-key... Let me look at the `Join` struct more carefully.

Actually, looking at the `Join` struct at line 3792, it has a single `null_equality: NullEquality`. So it's per-join, not per-key.

The fix should be: in the consumer, when we encounter mixed null semantics, we should keep the `Eq` columns as join keys and move the `IsNotDistinctFrom` columns to the filter. This way:
- Join keys with `NullEqualsNothing` correctly handle `Eq` semantics
- The `IsNotDistinctFrom` expressions in the filter preserve their null-equal semantics

    18	//! [`ExtractEquijoinPredicate`] identifies equality join (equijoin) predicates
    19	use crate::optimizer::ApplyOrder;
    20	use crate::{OptimizerConfig, OptimizerRule};
    21	use datafusion_common::tree_node::Transformed;
    22	use datafusion_common::{DFSchema, assert_or_internal_err};
    23	use datafusion_common::{NullEquality, Result};
    24	use datafusion_expr::utils::split_conjunction_owned;
    25	use datafusion_expr::utils::{can_hash, find_valid_equijoin_key_pair};
    26	use datafusion_expr::{BinaryExpr, Expr, ExprSchemable, Join, LogicalPlan, Operator};
    27	// equijoin predicate
    28	type EquijoinPredicate = (Expr, Expr);
    29	
    30	/// Optimizer that splits conjunctive join predicates into equijoin
    31	/// predicates and (other) filter predicates.
    32	///
    33	/// Join algorithms are often highly optimized for equality predicates such as `x = y`,
    34	/// often called `equijoin` predicates, so it is important to locate such predicates
    35	/// and treat them specially.
    36	///
    37	/// For example, `SELECT ... FROM A JOIN B ON (A.x = B.y AND B.z > 50)`
    38	/// has one equijoin predicate (`A.x = B.y`) and one filter predicate (`B.z > 50`).
    39	/// See [find_valid_equijoin_key_pair] for more information on what predicates
    40	/// are considered equijoins.
    41	#[derive(Default, Debug)]
    42	pub struct ExtractEquijoinPredicate;
    43	
    44	impl ExtractEquijoinPredicate {
    45	    #[expect(missing_docs)]
    46	    pub fn new() -> Self {
    47	        Self {}
    48	    }
    49	}
    50	
    51	impl OptimizerRule for ExtractEquijoinPredicate {
    52	    fn supports_rewrite(&self) -> bool {
    53	        true
    54	    }
    55	
    56	    fn name(&self) -> &str {
    57	        "extract_equijoin_predicate"
    58	    }
    59	
    60	    fn apply_order(&self) -> Option<ApplyOrder> {
    61	        Some(ApplyOrder::BottomUp)
    62	    }
    63	
    64	    fn rewrite(
    65	        &self,
    66	        plan: LogicalPlan,
    67	        _config: &dyn OptimizerConfig,
    68	    ) -> Result<Transformed<LogicalPlan>> {
    69	        match plan {
    70	            LogicalPlan::Join(Join {
    71	                left,
    72	                right,
    73	                mut on,
    74	                filter: Some(expr),
    75	                join_type,
    76	                join_constraint,
    77	                schema,
    78	                null_equality,
    79	                null_aware,
    80	            }) => {
    81	                let left_schema = left.schema();
    82	                let right_schema = right.schema();
    83	                let (equijoin_predicates, non_equijoin_expr) =
    84	                    split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate(expr, left_schema, right_schema)?;
    85	
    86	                // Equi-join operators like HashJoin support a special behavior
    87	                // that evaluates `NULL = NULL` as true instead of NULL. Therefore,
    88	                // we transform `t1.c1 IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.c1` into an equi-join
    89	                // and set the `NullEquality` configuration in the join operator.
    90	                // This allows certain queries to use Hash Join instead of
    91	                // Nested Loop Join, resulting in better performance.
    92	                //
    93	                // Only convert when there are NO equijoin predicates, to be conservative.
    94	                if on.is_empty()
    95	                    && equijoin_predicates.is_empty()
    96	                    && non_equijoin_expr.is_some()
    97	                {
    98	                    // SAFETY: checked in the outer `if`
    99	                    let expr = non_equijoin_expr.clone().unwrap();
   100	                    let (equijoin_predicates, non_equijoin_expr) =
   101	                        split_is_not_distinct_from_and_other_join_predicate(
   102	                            expr,
   103	                            left_schema,
   104	                            right_schema,
   105	                        )?;
   106	
   107	                    if !equijoin_predicates.is_empty() {
   108	                        on.extend(equijoin_predicates);
   109	
   110	                        return Ok(Transformed::yes(LogicalPlan::Join(Join {
   111	                            left,
   112	                            right,
   113	                            on,
   114	                            filter: non_equijoin_expr,
   115	                            join_type,
   116	                            join_constraint,
   117	                            schema,
   118	                            // According to `is not distinct from`'s semantics, it's
   119	                            // safe to override it
   120	                            null_equality: NullEquality::NullEqualsNull,
   121	                            null_aware,
   122	                        })));
   123	                    }
   124	                }
   125	
   126	                if !equijoin_predicates.is_empty() {
   127	                    on.extend(equijoin_predicates);
   128	                    Ok(Transformed::yes(LogicalPlan::Join(Join {
   129	                        left,
   130	                        right,
   131	                        on,
   132	                        filter: non_equijoin_expr,
   133	                        join_type,
   134	                        join_constraint,
   135	                        schema,
   136	                        null_equality,
   137	                        null_aware,
   138	                    })))
   139	                } else {
   140	                    Ok(Transformed::no(LogicalPlan::Join(Join {
   141	                        left,
   142	                        right,
   143	                        on,
   144	                        filter: non_equijoin_expr,
   145	                        join_type,
   146	                        join_constraint,
   147	                        schema,
   148	                        null_equality,
   149	                        null_aware,
   150	                    })))
   151	                }
   152	            }
   153	            _ => Ok(Transformed::no(plan)),
   154	        }
   155	    }
   156	}
   157	
   158	/// Splits an ANDed filter expression into equijoin predicates and remaining filters.
   159	/// Returns all equijoin predicates and the remaining filters combined with AND.
   160	///
   161	/// # Example
   162	///
   163	/// For the expression `a.id = b.id AND a.x > 10 AND b.x > b.id`, this function will extract `a.id = b.id` as an equijoin predicate.
   164	///
   165	/// It first splits the ANDed sub-expressions:
   166	/// - expr1: a.id = b.id
   167	/// - expr2: a.x > 10
   168	/// - expr3: b.x > b.id
   169	///
   170	/// Then, it filters out the equijoin predicates and collects the non-equality expressions.
   171	/// The equijoin condition is:
   172	/// - It is an equality expression like `lhs == rhs`
   173	/// - All column references in `lhs` are from the left schema, and all in `rhs` are from the right schema
   174	///
   175	/// According to the above rule, `expr1` is the equijoin predicate, while `expr2` and `expr3` are not.
   176	/// The function returns Ok(\[expr1\], Some(expr2 AND expr3))
   177	fn split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate(
   178	    filter: Expr,
   179	    left_schema: &DFSchema,
   180	    right_schema: &DFSchema,
   181	) -> Result<(Vec<EquijoinPredicate>, Option<Expr>)> {
   182	    split_op_and_other_join_predicates(filter, left_schema, right_schema, Operator::Eq)
   183	}
   184	
   185	/// See `split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate`'s comment for the idea. This function
   186	/// is splitting out `is not distinct from` expressions instead of equal exprs.
   187	/// The `is not distinct from` exprs will be return as `EquijoinPredicate`.
   188	///
   189	/// # Example
   190	/// - Input: `a.id IS NOT DISTINCT FROM b.id AND a.x > 10 AND b.x > b.id`
   191	/// - Output from this splitter: `Ok([a.id, b.id], Some((a.x > 10) AND (b.x > b.id)))`
   192	///
   193	/// # Note
   194	/// Caller should be cautious -- `is not distinct from` is not equivalent to an
   195	/// equal expression; the caller is responsible for correctly setting the
   196	/// `nulls equals nulls` property in the join operator (if it supports it) to
   197	/// make the transformation valid.
   198	///
   199	/// For the above example: in downstream, a valid plan that uses the extracted
   200	/// equijoin keys should look like:
   201	///
   202	/// HashJoin
   203	/// - on: `a.id = b.id` (equality)
   204	/// - join_filter: `(a.x > 10) AND (b.x > b.id)`
   205	/// - nulls_equals_null: `true`
   206	///
   207	/// This reflects that `IS NOT DISTINCT FROM` treats `NULL = NULL` as true and
   208	/// thus requires setting `NullEquality::NullEqualsNull` in the join operator to
   209	/// preserve semantics while enabling an equi-join implementation (e.g., HashJoin).
   210	fn split_is_not_distinct_from_and_other_join_predicate(
   211	    filter: Expr,
   212	    left_schema: &DFSchema,
   213	    right_schema: &DFSchema,
   214	) -> Result<(Vec<EquijoinPredicate>, Option<Expr>)> {
   215	    split_op_and_other_join_predicates(
   216	        filter,
   217	        left_schema,
   218	        right_schema,
   219	        Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
   220	    )
   221	}
   222	
   223	/// See comments in `split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate` for details.
   224	fn split_op_and_other_join_predicates(
   225	    filter: Expr,
   226	    left_schema: &DFSchema,
   227	    right_schema: &DFSchema,
   228	    operator: Operator,
   229	) -> Result<(Vec<EquijoinPredicate>, Option<Expr>)> {
   230	    assert_or_internal_err!(
   231	        matches!(operator, Operator::Eq | Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom),
   232	        "split_op_and_other_join_predicates only supports 'Eq' or 'IsNotDistinctFrom' operators, \
   233	        but received: {:?}",
   234	        operator
   235	    );
   236	
   237	    let exprs = split_conjunction_owned(filter);
   238	
   239	    // Treat 'is not distinct from' comparison as join key in equal joins
   240	    let mut accum_join_keys: Vec<(Expr, Expr)> = vec![];
   241	    let mut accum_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];
   242	    for expr in exprs {
   243	        match expr {
   244	            Expr::BinaryExpr(BinaryExpr {
   245	                ref left,
   246	                ref op,
   247	                ref right,
   248	            }) if *op == operator => {
   249	                let join_key_pair =
   250	                    find_valid_equijoin_key_pair(left, right, left_schema, right_schema)?;
   251	
   252	                if let Some((left_expr, right_expr)) = join_key_pair {
   253	                    let left_expr_type = left_expr.get_type(left_schema)?;
   254	                    let right_expr_type = right_expr.get_type(right_schema)?;
   255	
   256	                    if can_hash(&left_expr_type) && can_hash(&right_expr_type) {
   257	                        accum_join_keys.push((left_expr, right_expr));
   258	                    } else {
   259	                        accum_filters.push(expr);
   260	                    }
   261	                } else {
   262	                    accum_filters.push(expr);
   263	                }
   264	            }
   265	            _ => accum_filters.push(expr),
   266	        }
   267	    }
   268	
   269	    let result_filter = accum_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
   270	    Ok((accum_join_keys, result_filter))
   271	}
   272

   399	    fn join_with_and_or_filter() -> Result<()> {
   400	        let t1 = test_table_scan_with_name("t1")?;
   401	        let t2 = test_table_scan_with_name("t2")?;
   402	
   403	        let plan = LogicalPlanBuilder::from(t1)
   404	            .join_on(
   405	                t2,
   406	                JoinType::Left,
   407	                Some(
   408	                    col("t1.c")
   409	                        .eq(col("t2.c"))
   410	                        .or((col("t1.a") + col("t1.b")).gt(col("t2.b") + col("t2.c")))
   411	                        .and(
   412	                            col("t1.a").eq(col("t2.a")).and(col("t1.b").eq(col("t2.b"))),
   413	                        ),
   414	                ),
   415	            )?
   416	            .build()?;
   417	
   418	        assert_optimized_plan_equal!(
   419	            plan,
   420	            @r"
   421	        Left Join: t1.a = t2.a, t1.b = t2.b Filter: t1.c = t2.c OR t1.a + t1.b > t2.b + t2.c [a:UInt32, b:UInt32, c:UInt32, a:UInt32;N, b:UInt32;N, c:UInt32;N]
   422	          TableScan: t1 [a:UInt32, b:UInt32, c:UInt32]
   423	          TableScan: t2 [a:UInt32, b:UInt32, c:UInt32]
   424	        "
   425	        )
   426	    }

    77	        } else {
    78	            unreachable!()
    79	        }
    80	    }
    81	}
    82	
    83	#[derive(Debug, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)]
    84	struct MockUserDefinedLogicalPlan {
    85	    /// Replacement for serialize/deserialize data
    86	    validation_bytes: Vec<u8>,
    87	    inputs: Vec<LogicalPlan>,
    88	    empty_schema: DFSchemaRef,
    89	}
    90	
    91	// `PartialOrd` needed for `UserDefinedLogicalNodeCore`, manual implementation necessary due to
    92	// the `empty_schema` field.
    93	impl PartialOrd for MockUserDefinedLogicalPlan {
    94	    fn partial_cmp(&self, other: &Self) -> Option<Ordering> {
    95	        match self.validation_bytes.partial_cmp(&other.validation_bytes) {
    96	            Some(Ordering::Equal) => self.inputs.partial_cmp(&other.inputs),
    97	            cmp => cmp,
    98	        }
    99	        // TODO (https://github.com/apache/datafusion/issues/17477) avoid recomparing all fields
   100	        .filter(|cmp| *cmp != Ordering::Equal || self == other)
   101	    }
   102	}
   103	
   104	impl UserDefinedLogicalNode for MockUserDefinedLogicalPlan {
   105	    fn as_any(&self) -> &dyn std::any::Any {
   106	        self
   107	    }
   108	
   109	    fn name(&self) -> &str {
   110	        "MockUserDefinedLogicalPlan"
   111	    }
   112	
   113	    fn inputs(&self) -> Vec<&LogicalPlan> {
   114	        self.inputs.iter().collect()
   115	    }
   116	
   117	    fn schema(&self) -> &DFSchemaRef {
   118	        &self.empty_schema
   119	    }
   120	
   121	    fn check_invariants(&self, _check: InvariantLevel) -> Result<()> {
   122	        Ok(())
   123	    }
   124	
   125	    fn expressions(&self) -> Vec<Expr> {
   126	        vec![]
   127	    }
   128	
   129	    fn fmt_for_explain(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter) -> std::fmt::Result {
   130	        write!(
   131	            f,
   132	            "MockUserDefinedLogicalPlan [validation_bytes={:?}]",
   133	            self.validation_bytes
   134	        )
   135	    }
   136	
   137	    fn with_exprs_and_inputs(
   138	        &self,
   139	        _: Vec<Expr>,
   140	        inputs: Vec<LogicalPlan>,
   141	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn UserDefinedLogicalNode>> {
   142	        Ok(Arc::new(Self {
   143	            validation_bytes: self.validation_bytes.clone(),
   144	            inputs,
   145	            empty_schema: Arc::new(DFSchema::empty()),
   146	        }))
   147	    }
   148	
   149	    fn dyn_hash(&self, _: &mut dyn std::hash::Hasher) {
   150	        unimplemented!()
   151	    }
   152	
   153	    fn dyn_eq(&self, _: &dyn UserDefinedLogicalNode) -> bool {
   154	        unimplemented!()
   155	    }
   156	
   157	    fn dyn_ord(&self, _: &dyn UserDefinedLogicalNode) -> Option<Ordering> {
   158	        unimplemented!()
   159	    }
   160	
   161	    fn supports_limit_pushdown(&self) -> bool {
   162	        false // Disallow limit push-down by default
   163	    }
   164	}
   165	
   166	impl MockUserDefinedLogicalPlan {
   167	    pub fn new(validation_bytes: Vec<u8>) -> Self {
   168	        Self {
   169	            validation_bytes,
   170	            inputs: vec![],
   171	            empty_schema: Arc::new(DFSchema::empty()),
   172	        }
   173	    }
   174	
   175	    fn serialize(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>> {
   176	        Ok(self.validation_bytes.clone())
   177	    }
   178	
   179	    fn deserialize(bytes: &[u8]) -> Result<Arc<dyn UserDefinedLogicalNode>>
   180	    where
   181	        Self: Sized,
   182	    {
   183	        Ok(Arc::new(MockUserDefinedLogicalPlan::new(bytes.to_vec())))
   184	    }
   185	}

   216	async fn roundtrip_subquery_with_empty_relation() -> Result<()> {
   217	    // Test EmptyRelation in the context of scalar subqueries.
   218	    // The optimizer may simplify the subquery away, but we're testing that
   219	    // the EmptyRelation round-trips correctly when it appears in the plan.
   220	    let ctx = create_context().await?;
   221	    let df = ctx.sql("SELECT (SELECT 1) as nested").await?;
   222	    let plan = df.into_optimized_plan()?;
   223	
   224	    // Just verify the round-trip succeeds and produces valid results
   225	    let proto = to_substrait_plan(&plan, &ctx.state())?;
   226	    let plan2 = from_substrait_plan(&ctx.state(), &proto).await?;
   227	    let df2 = DataFrame::new(ctx.state(), plan2);
   228	    df2.show().await?;
   229	    Ok(())
   230	}

   266	#[tokio::test]
   267	async fn select_with_reused_functions() -> Result<()> {
   268	    let ctx = create_context().await?;
   269	    let sql = "SELECT * FROM data WHERE a > 1 AND a < 10 AND b > 0";
   270	    let proto = roundtrip_with_ctx(sql, ctx).await?;
   271	    let mut functions = proto
   272	        .extensions
   273	        .iter()
   274	        .map(|e| match e.mapping_type.as_ref().unwrap() {
   275	            MappingType::ExtensionFunction(ext_f) => {
   276	                (ext_f.function_anchor, ext_f.name.to_owned())
   277	            }
   278	            _ => unreachable!("Non-function extensions not expected"),
   279	        })
   280	        .collect::<Vec<_>>();
   281	    functions.sort_by_key(|(anchor, _)| *anchor);
   282	
   283	    // Functions are encountered (and thus registered) depth-first
   284	    let expected = vec![
   285	        (0, "gt".to_string()),
   286	        (1, "lt".to_string()),
   287	        (2, "and".to_string()),
   288	    ];
   289	    assert_eq!(functions, expected);
   290	
   291	    Ok(())
   292	}

   360	        TableScan: data projection=[a, b, c, e]

   400	        TableScan: data projection=[a, b]
   401	    "

   490	
   491	// Test that DataFusion functions gets correctly mapped to Substrait names (when the names are different)
   492	// Follows the same structure as existing roundtrip tests, but more explicitly tests for name mappings
   493	async fn test_substrait_to_df_name_mapping(
   494	    substrait_name: &str,
   495	    sql: &str,
   496	) -> Result<()> {
   497	    let ctx = create_context().await?;
   498	    let df = ctx.sql(sql).await?;
   499	    let plan = df.into_optimized_plan()?;
   500	    let proto = to_substrait_plan(&plan, &ctx.state())?;
   501	
   502	    let function_name = match proto.extensions[0].mapping_type.as_ref().unwrap() {
   503	        MappingType::ExtensionFunction(ext_f) => &ext_f.name,
   504	        _ => unreachable!("Expected function extension"),
   505	    };
   506	
   507	    assert_eq!(function_name, substrait_name);
   508	
   509	    let plan2 = from_substrait_plan(&ctx.state(), &proto).await?;
   510	    let plan2 = ctx.state().optimize(&plan2)?;
   511	
   512	    let plan1str = format!("{plan}");
   513	    let plan2str = format!("{plan2}");
   514	    assert_eq!(plan1str, plan2str);
   515	
   516	    assert_eq!(plan.schema(), plan2.schema());
   517	
   518	    Ok(())
   519	}

Now I have enough context. Let me think about the fix properly.

The core issue is in `split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality`:

```rust
fn split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality(
    filter: &Expr,
) -> (Vec<(Column, Column)>, bool, Option<Expr>) {
    let exprs = split_conjunction(filter);
    let mut accum_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
    let mut accum_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];
    let mut nulls_equal_nulls = false;

    for expr in exprs {
        match expr {
            Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
                x @ (BinaryExpr { left, op: Operator::Eq, right }
                | BinaryExpr { left, op: Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom, right }) => {
                    nulls_equal_nulls = match x.op {
                        Operator::Eq => false,
                        Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom => true,
                        _ => unreachable!(),
                    };
                    // ...
                }
                _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
            },
            _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
        }
    }
    // ...
}
```

The `nulls_equal_nulls` is overwritten on each iteration, so only the last operator's semantics are used.

Since DataFusion's `Join` struct only supports a single `null_equality` for all join keys, we need to decide what to do when there are mixed semantics.

Looking at how the producer works: it uses a single `eq_op` for all join keys, so a roundtrip of a plan that originally had mixed semantics can't be perfect. But we need to handle consuming plans that come from other sources.

The best approach: when all keys have the same null semantics, use that. When mixed:
- Use `NullEqualsNothing` for the join (safe default)
- Move the `IsNotDistinctFrom` keys to the filter (preserving their null-equal semantics)

Actually wait, let me reconsider. If we have:
- key1: `Eq` (null equals nothing)
- key2: `IsNotDistinctFrom` (null equals null)

And we set join to `NullEqualsNothing`:
- key1 is handled correctly
- key2 would be handled incorrectly (null equals nothing instead of null equals null)

So we need to move key2 to the filter. But if we move key2 to the filter, it becomes a post-join filter which might not be equivalent for outer joins.

Alternative: Use `NullEqualsNull` for the join, and wrap the `Eq` key expressions in something that filters out nulls. But that's complicated.

Actually, the simplest correct approach: 
- If all join keys have the same null semantics, use it
- If mixed, we can't represent it perfectly. We should use `NullEqualsNull` (the more permissive) and add filter conditions for the `Eq` keys that exclude NULLs. But this is also complex.

Wait, let me look again at the PR description:

> If a join with join_keys having mixed null handling i.e. a few join keys with `NullEqNull` and a few with `NullEqNothing` then the resulting outer join should preserve these semantics

The expected behavior is to preserve the semantics. Since DataFusion's Join only has a single null_equality, the fix might be different than what I'm thinking. Let me check if there are any pending changes to the `Join` struct to support per-key null equality...

Actually, let me re-read the code more carefully. The function returns `(Vec<(Column, Column)>, bool, Option<Expr>)` - a single bool. The caller then uses that single bool to set `null_equality`. 

But looking at the problem from a different angle: maybe the fix should be to NOT split `IsNotDistinctFrom` into join keys at all, and instead keep them in the filter. Because the join keys with `Eq` have different semantics from `IsNotDistinctFrom`. 

Wait, but the current code already puts both `Eq` and `IsNotDistinctFrom` into join keys. The only problem is that it uses the last one's null semantics for all.

Let me look at how the physical plan handles null_equality. If `NullEquality::NullEqualsNull`, then `null == null` is treated as `true` (like `IS NOT DISTINCT FROM`). If `NullEquality::NullEqualsNothing`, then `null == anything` is `null`.

So the correct approach for mixed semantics:
1. If we have both `Eq` and `IsNotDistinctFrom` keys, we should split them:
   - `Eq` keys go to join keys with `NullEqualsNothing`
   - `IsNotDistinctFrom` keys go to filter (since we can't have per-key null semantics)
   
   OR:
   
   - All keys go to join keys with `NullEqualsNull` (treating all as IS NOT DISTINCT FROM) 
   - Add filter: `(key IS NOT NULL)` for the `Eq` keys to make them behave like `Eq`

But the first approach is simpler and more commonly correct.

Actually, wait. Let me look at the extract_equijoin_predicate optimizer to see how it handles this case. In that optimizer (lines 94-123), it only converts `IsNotDistinctFrom` to join keys when there are NO existing equijoin predicates. If there ARE equijoin predicates, it keeps the `IsNotDistinctFrom` in the filter.

So the optimizer's approach is: if mixed, keep `Eq` as join keys and `IsNotDistinctFrom` in filter.

That seems like the right approach for the consumer too! When we encounter mixed semantics:
- Keep `Eq` keys as join keys
- Move `IsNotDistinctFrom` keys to the filter

OR, we could do what the optimizer does when there are ONLY `IsNotDistinctFrom` keys: use `NullEqualsNull` for join keys.

Let me implement this:

1. Check if all keys have the same null semantics
2. If yes, use that
3. If mixed (some `Eq`, some `IsNotDistinctFrom`), keep `Eq` keys as join keys and move `IsNotDistinctFrom` to filter, using `NullEqualsNothing`

}' --new_str 'fn split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality(
    filter: &Expr,
) -> (Vec<(Column, Column)>, bool, Option<Expr>) {
    let exprs = split_conjunction(filter);

    let mut accum_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
    let mut accum_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];
    // Track whether we have seen Eq (null equals nothing) and IsNotDistinctFrom (null equals null) keys
    let mut has_eq_keys = false;
    let mut has_null_eq_null_keys = false;

    for expr in exprs {
        #[expect(clippy::collapsible_match)]
        match expr {
            Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
                BinaryExpr {
                    left,
                    op: op @ Operator::Eq,
                    right,
                }
                | BinaryExpr {
                    left,
                    op: op @ Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
                    right,
                } => {
                    let is_null_eq_null = matches!(op, Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom);
                    if is_null_eq_null {
                        has_null_eq_null_keys = true;
                    } else {
                        has_eq_keys = true;
                    }

                    match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
                        (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
                            accum_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
                        }
                        _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                    }
                }
                _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
            },
            _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
        }
    }

    // If we have mixed null semantics (both Eq and IsNotDistinctFrom keys),
    // we cannot represent this with a single null_equality per join.
    // In this case, we keep the Eq keys as join keys and move the
    // IsNotDistinctFrom keys to the filter to preserve their semantics.
    if has_eq_keys && has_null_eq_null_keys {
        let mut new_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
        let mut new_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];

        for (l, r) in accum_join_keys {
            // Check if this key was originally an IsNotDistinctFrom by looking for it
            // in the original expressions. We need to rebuild the filter expressions.
            // Actually, we need to look at the original exprs again to determine which
            // keys came from IsNotDistinctFrom.
            // For simplicity, we'"'"'ll re-process: Eq keys stay as join keys,
            // IsNotDistinctFrom keys become filter expressions.
        }

        // Re-process: we go through the original exprs again
        let mut final_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
        let mut final_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];

        for expr in exprs {
            match expr {
                Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
                    BinaryExpr {
                        left,
                        op: Operator::Eq,
                        right,
                    } => {
                        match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
                            (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
                                final_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
                            }
                            _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                        }
                    }
                    BinaryExpr {
                        left,
                        op: Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
                        right,
                    } => {
                        // Move IsNotDistinctFrom expressions to filter
                        final_filters.push(expr.clone());
                    }
                    _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                },
                _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
            }
        }

        let join_filter = final_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
        (final_join_keys, false, join_filter)
    } else {
        // All keys have the same null semantics (or there are no keys)
        let nulls_equal_nulls = has_null_eq_null_keys;
        let join_filter = accum_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
        (accum_join_keys, nulls_equal_nulls, join_filter)
    }

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/datafusion/substrait/src/logical_plan/consumer/rel/join_rel.rs   --old_str 'fn split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality(
    filter: &Expr,
) -> (Vec<(Column, Column)>, bool, Option<Expr>) {
    let exprs = split_conjunction(filter);

    let mut accum_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
    let mut accum_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];
    // Track whether we have seen Eq (null equals nothing) and IsNotDistinctFrom (null equals null) keys
    let mut has_eq_keys = false;
    let mut has_null_eq_null_keys = false;

    for expr in exprs {
        #[expect(clippy::collapsible_match)]
        match expr {
            Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
                BinaryExpr {
                    left,
                    op: op @ Operator::Eq,
                    right,
                }
                | BinaryExpr {
                    left,
                    op: op @ Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
                    right,
                } => {
                    let is_null_eq_null = matches!(op, Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom);
                    if is_null_eq_null {
                        has_null_eq_null_keys = true;
                    } else {
                        has_eq_keys = true;
                    }

                    match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
                        (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
                            accum_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
                        }
                        _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                    }
                }
                _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
            },
            _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
        }
    }

    // If we have mixed null semantics (both Eq and IsNotDistinctFrom keys),
    // we cannot represent this with a single null_equality per join.
    // In this case, we keep the Eq keys as join keys and move the
    // IsNotDistinctFrom keys to the filter to preserve their semantics.
    if has_eq_keys && has_null_eq_null_keys {
        let mut new_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
        let mut new_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];

        for (l, r) in accum_join_keys {
            // Check if this key was originally an IsNotDistinctFrom by looking for it
            // in the original expressions. We need to rebuild the filter expressions.
            // Actually, we need to look at the original exprs again to determine which
            // keys came from IsNotDistinctFrom.
            // For simplicity, we'"'"'ll re-process: Eq keys stay as join keys,
            // IsNotDistinctFrom keys become filter expressions.
        }

        // Re-process: we go through the original exprs again
        let mut final_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
        let mut final_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];

        for expr in exprs {
            match expr {
                Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
                    BinaryExpr {
                        left,
                        op: Operator::Eq,
                        right,
                    } => {
                        match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
                            (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
                                final_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
                            }
                            _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                        }
                    }
                    BinaryExpr {
                        left,
                        op: Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
                        right,
                    } => {
                        // Move IsNotDistinctFrom expressions to filter
                        final_filters.push(expr.clone());
                    }
                    _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                },
                _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
            }
        }

        let join_filter = final_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
        (final_join_keys, false, join_filter)
    } else {
        // All keys have the same null semantics (or there are no keys)
        let nulls_equal_nulls = has_null_eq_null_keys;
        let join_filter = accum_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
        (accum_join_keys, nulls_equal_nulls, join_filter)
    }
}' --new_str 'fn split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality(
    filter: &Expr,
) -> (Vec<(Column, Column)>, bool, Option<Expr>) {
    let exprs = split_conjunction(filter);

    let mut accum_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
    let mut accum_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];
    // Track whether we have seen Eq (null equals nothing) and IsNotDistinctFrom (null equals null) keys
    let mut has_eq_keys = false;
    let mut has_null_eq_null_keys = false;

    for expr in exprs {
        #[expect(clippy::collapsible_match)]
        match expr {
            Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
                BinaryExpr {
                    left,
                    op: op @ Operator::Eq,
                    right,
                }
                | BinaryExpr {
                    left,
                    op: op @ Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
                    right,
                } => {
                    let is_null_eq_null = matches!(op, Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom);
                    if is_null_eq_null {
                        has_null_eq_null_keys = true;
                    } else {
                        has_eq_keys = true;
                    }

                    match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
                        (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
                            accum_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
                        }
                        _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                    }
                }
                _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
            },
            _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
        }
    }

    // If we have mixed null semantics (both Eq and IsNotDistinctFrom keys),
    // we cannot represent this with a single null_equality per join.
    // In this case, we keep the Eq keys as join keys with NullEqualsNothing
    // and move the IsNotDistinctFrom keys to the filter to preserve their
    // null-equal semantics.
    if has_eq_keys && has_null_eq_null_keys {
        let mut final_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
        let mut final_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];

        for (l, r) in accum_join_keys {
            // Check if this key was originally an IsNotDistinctFrom by
            // looking at the original expression. We rebuild the
            // IsNotDistinctFrom expression and add it to the filter.
            let is_null_eq_null_key = accum_join_keys.iter().any(|(jl, jr)| {
                // We need to determine which operator each join key came from.
                // Since we don'"'"'t have that info, we re-derive by checking
                // if this pair appears as an IsNotDistinctFrom in the
                // original expressions.
                false // placeholder, we'"'"'ll use a different approach
            });
        }

        // Re-process the original expressions: Eq column pairs become join keys,
        // IsNotDistinctFrom expressions go to filter, other expressions stay as filter.
        let mut final_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
        let mut final_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];

        for expr in exprs {
            match expr {
                Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
                    BinaryExpr {
                        left,
                        op: Operator::Eq,
                        right,
                    } => {
                        match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
                            (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
                                final_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
                            }
                            _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                        }
                    }
                    BinaryExpr {
                        left: _,
                        op: Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
                        right: _,
                    } => {
                        // Move IsNotDistinctFrom expressions to filter
                        final_filters.push(expr.clone());
                    }
                    _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                },
                _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
            }
        }

        let join_filter = final_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
        (final_join_keys, false, join_filter)
    } else {
        // All keys have the same null semantics (or there are no keys)
        let nulls_equal_nulls = has_null_eq_null_keys;
        let join_filter = accum_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
        (accum_join_keys, nulls_equal_nulls, join_filter)
    }

    filter: &Expr,
) -> (Vec<(Column, Column)>, bool, Option<Expr>) {
    let exprs = split_conjunction(filter);

    let mut accum_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
    let mut accum_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];
    // Track whether we have seen Eq (null equals nothing) and IsNotDistinctFrom (null equals null) keys
    let mut has_eq_keys = false;
    let mut has_null_eq_null_keys = false;

    for expr in exprs {
        #[expect(clippy::collapsible_match)]
        match expr {
            Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
                BinaryExpr {
                    left,
                    op: op @ Operator::Eq,
                    right,
                }
                | BinaryExpr {
                    left,
                    op: op @ Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
                    right,
                } => {
                    let is_null_eq_null = matches!(op, Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom);
                    if is_null_eq_null {
                        has_null_eq_null_keys = true;
                    } else {
                        has_eq_keys = true;
                    }

                    match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
                        (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
                            accum_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
                        }
                        _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                    }
                }
                _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
            },
            _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
        }
    }

    // If we have mixed null semantics (both Eq and IsNotDistinctFrom keys),
    // we cannot represent this with a single null_equality per join.
    // In this case, we keep the Eq keys as join keys with NullEqualsNothing
    // and move the IsNotDistinctFrom keys to the filter to preserve their
    // null-equal semantics.
    if has_eq_keys && has_null_eq_null_keys {
        let mut final_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
        let mut final_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];

        for (l, r) in accum_join_keys {
            // Check if this key was originally an IsNotDistinctFrom by
            // looking at the original expression. We rebuild the
            // IsNotDistinctFrom expression and add it to the filter.
            let is_null_eq_null_key = accum_join_keys.iter().any(|(jl, jr)| {
                // We need to determine which operator each join key came from.
                // Since we don'"'"'t have that info, we re-derive by checking
                // if this pair appears as an IsNotDistinctFrom in the
                // original expressions.
                false // placeholder, we'"'"'ll use a different approach
            });
        }

        // Re-process the original expressions: Eq column pairs become join keys,
        // IsNotDistinctFrom expressions go to filter, other expressions stay as filter.
        let mut final_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
        let mut final_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];

        for expr in exprs {
            match expr {
                Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
                    BinaryExpr {
                        left,
                        op: Operator::Eq,
                        right,
                    } => {
                        match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
                            (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
                                final_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
                            }
                            _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                        }
                    }
                    BinaryExpr {
                        left: _,
                        op: Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
                        right: _,
                    } => {
                        // Move IsNotDistinctFrom expressions to filter
                        final_filters.push(expr.clone());
                    }
                    _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
                },
                _ => final_filters.push(expr.clone()),
            }
        }

        let join_filter = final_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
        (final_join_keys, false, join_filter)
    } else {
        // All keys have the same null semantics (or there are no keys)
        let nulls_equal_nulls = has_null_eq_null_keys;
        let join_filter = accum_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
        (accum_join_keys, nulls_equal_nulls, join_filter)
    }

    18	use crate::logical_plan::consumer::SubstraitConsumer;
    19	use datafusion::common::{Column, JoinType, NullEquality, not_impl_err, plan_err};
    20	use datafusion::logical_expr::requalify_sides_if_needed;
    21	use datafusion::logical_expr::utils::split_conjunction;

    26	use substrait::proto::{JoinRel, join_rel};
    27	
    28	pub async fn from_join_rel(
    29	    consumer: &impl SubstraitConsumer,
    30	    join: &JoinRel,
    31	) -> datafusion::common::Result<LogicalPlan> {
    32	    if join.post_join_filter.is_some() {
    33	        return not_impl_err!("JoinRel with post_join_filter is not yet supported");
    34	    }
    35	
    36	    let left: LogicalPlanBuilder = LogicalPlanBuilder::from(
    37	        consumer.consume_rel(join.left.as_ref().unwrap()).await?,
    38	    );
    39	    let right = LogicalPlanBuilder::from(
    40	        consumer.consume_rel(join.right.as_ref().unwrap()).await?,
    41	    );
    42	    let (left, right, _requalified) = requalify_sides_if_needed(left, right)?;
    43	
    44	    let join_type = from_substrait_jointype(join.r#type)?;
    45	    // The join condition expression needs full input schema and not the output schema from join since we lose columns from
    46	    // certain join types such as semi and anti joins
    47	    let in_join_schema = left.schema().join(right.schema())?;
    48	
    49	    // If join expression exists, parse the `on` condition expression, build join and return
    50	    // Otherwise, build join with only the filter, without join keys
    51	    match &join.expression.as_ref() {
    52	        Some(expr) => {
    53	            let on = consumer.consume_expression(expr, &in_join_schema).await?;
    54	            // The join expression can contain both equal and non-equal ops.
    55	            // As of datafusion 31.0.0, the equal and non equal join conditions are in separate fields.
    56	            // So we extract each part as follows:
    57	            // - If an Eq or IsNotDistinctFrom op is encountered, add the left column, right column and is_null_equal_nulls to `join_ons` vector
    58	            // - Otherwise we add the expression to join_filter (use conjunction if filter already exists)
    59	            let (join_ons, nulls_equal_nulls, join_filter) =
    60	                split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality(&on);
    61	            let (left_cols, right_cols): (Vec<_>, Vec<_>) =
    62	                itertools::multiunzip(join_ons);
    63	            let null_equality = if nulls_equal_nulls {
    64	                NullEquality::NullEqualsNull
    65	            } else {
    66	                NullEquality::NullEqualsNothing
    67	            };
    68	            left.join_detailed(
    69	                right.build()?,
    70	                join_type,
    71	                (left_cols, right_cols),
    72	                join_filter,
    73	                null_equality,
    74	            )?
    75	            .build()
    76	        }
    77	        None => {
    78	            let on: Vec<String> = vec![];
    79	            left.join_detailed(
    80	                right.build()?,
    81	                join_type,
    82	                (on.clone(), on),
    83	                None,
    84	                NullEquality::NullEqualsNothing,
    85	            )?
    86	            .build()
    87	        }
    88	    }
    89	}
    90	
    91	fn split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality(
    92	    filter: &Expr,
    93	) -> (Vec<(Column, Column)>, bool, Option<Expr>) {
    94	    let exprs = split_conjunction(filter);
    95	
    96	    // Track whether we have seen Eq (null equals nothing) and IsNotDistinctFrom (null equals null) keys
    97	    let mut has_eq_keys = false;
    98	    let mut has_null_eq_null_keys = false;
    99	
   100	    // First pass: detect if we have mixed null semantics
   101	    for expr in &exprs {
   102	        match expr {
   103	            Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
   104	                BinaryExpr {
   105	                    op: Operator::Eq, ..
   106	                } => has_eq_keys = true,
   107	                BinaryExpr {
   108	                    op: Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
   109	                    ..
   110	                } => has_null_eq_null_keys = true,
   111	                _ => {}
   112	            },
   113	            _ => {}
   114	        }
   115	    }
   116	
   117	    // If we have mixed null semantics (both Eq and IsNotDistinctFrom keys),
   118	    // we cannot represent this with a single null_equality per join.
   119	    // In this case, we keep the Eq keys as join keys with NullEqualsNothing
   120	    // and move the IsNotDistinctFrom keys to the filter to preserve their
   121	    // null-equal semantics.
   122	    let mixed_semantics = has_eq_keys && has_null_eq_null_keys;
   123	
   124	    let mut accum_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
   125	    let mut accum_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];
   126	
   127	    for expr in exprs {
   128	        #[expect(clippy::collapsible_match)]
   129	        match expr {
   130	            Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
   131	                BinaryExpr {
   132	                    left,
   133	                    op: Operator::Eq,
   134	                    right,
   135	                } => {
   136	                    match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
   137	                        (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
   138	                            accum_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
   139	                        }
   140	                        _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   141	                    }
   142	                }
   143	                BinaryExpr {
   144	                    left,
   145	                    op: Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
   146	                    right,
   147	                } => {
   148	                    if mixed_semantics {
   149	                        // Move IsNotDistinctFrom expressions to filter
   150	                        accum_filters.push(expr.clone());
   151	                    } else {
   152	                        match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
   153	                            (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
   154	                                accum_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
   155	                            }
   156	                            _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   157	                        }
   158	                    }
   159	                }
   160	                _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   161	            },
   162	            _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   163	        }
   164	    }
   165	
   166	    let nulls_equal_nulls = !mixed_semantics && has_null_eq_null_keys;
   167	    let join_filter = accum_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
   168	    (accum_join_keys, nulls_equal_nulls, join_filter)
   169	}
   170	
   171	fn from_substrait_jointype(join_type: i32) -> datafusion::common::Result<JoinType> {
   172	    if let Ok(substrait_join_type) = join_rel::JoinType::try_from(join_type) {
   173	        match substrait_join_type {
   174	            join_rel::JoinType::Inner => Ok(JoinType::Inner),
   175	            join_rel::JoinType::Left => Ok(JoinType::Left),
   176	            join_rel::JoinType::Right => Ok(JoinType::Right),
   177	            join_rel::JoinType::Outer => Ok(JoinType::Full),
   178	            join_rel::JoinType::LeftAnti => Ok(JoinType::LeftAnti),
   179	            join_rel::JoinType::LeftSemi => Ok(JoinType::LeftSemi),
   180	            join_rel::JoinType::LeftMark => Ok(JoinType::LeftMark),
   181	            join_rel::JoinType::RightMark => Ok(JoinType::RightMark),
   182	            join_rel::JoinType::RightAnti => Ok(JoinType::RightAnti),
   183	            join_rel::JoinType::RightSemi => Ok(JoinType::RightSemi),
   184	            _ => plan_err!("unsupported join type {substrait_join_type:?}"),
   185	        }
   186	    } else {
   187	        plan_err!("invalid join type variant {join_type}")
   188	    }

All 186 tests passed. Now let me think about edge cases and whether my fix is complete.

Wait, I need to reconsider my approach. The PR description says:

> If a join with join_keys having mixed null handling i.e. a few join keys with `NullEqNull` and a few with `NullEqNothing` then the resulting outer join should preserve these semantics

My current approach moves `IsNotDistinctFrom` to the filter when there are mixed semantics. But for outer joins, filter conditions are applied after the join, which changes semantics. For example:

```sql
SELECT * FROM t1 LEFT JOIN t2 ON t1.id = t2.id AND t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val
```

If we move `t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val` to the filter, then for left join, rows from t1 that don't have matching t2 rows will be filtered out (since the filter would evaluate to null/false for the null-padded t2 row). This is WRONG.

Hmm, but actually, let me check: does DataFusion's join apply the filter during join or after? Let me check the physical plan implementation...

Actually, looking at the `Join` struct:
- `on`: equijoin keys
- `filter`: non-equi conditions

The filter in `Join` is applied during the join, not after. Let me verify this...

2026-06-01 04:53:14,836 - INFO - swea-agent-apache__datafusion-21121 - 💭 THOUGHT
Looking at the nested loop join, the `join_filter` is applied during the join process, which is correct. For outer joins, the filter is still applied but the outer join semantics are preserved for non-matching rows. Let me check more...

Actually, looking at the code in `hash_join/exec.rs` line 1163 and related, the filter is applied during the join, not after. For outer joins, the filter is applied before determining if a row should be included as a null-padded row.

So my approach of moving `IsNotDistinctFrom` to the filter for mixed semantics should be correct for inner joins. For outer joins, it may change semantics. But wait, let me think about this more carefully...

For a LEFT JOIN:
- If we have `ON t1.id = t2.id AND t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val`
- Original: both conditions are part of the join condition
- My approach: `t1.id = t2.id` becomes join key, `t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val` becomes filter
- For matching rows: filter applies and works correctly
- For non-matching rows (t1 row with no t2 match): the left row is preserved with NULLs for right columns. The filter would evaluate `t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM NULL` which is FALSE (since `IS NOT DISTINCT FROM` returns false when one side is null and the other is not). So the left row would be filtered out, which is WRONG.

So my approach is NOT correct for outer joins.

Let me reconsider. What are the options?

1. Keep `IsNotDistinctFrom` as join keys with `NullEqualsNull` semantics, and for `Eq` keys, add a filter condition that excludes nulls. But that's complex and changes semantics.

2. Accept that we can't perfectly represent mixed semantics and choose the safer option.

Actually, let me re-look at the producer code. The producer uses a SINGLE operator for ALL join keys based on the null_equality. So when producing from DataFusion to Substrait, all keys become either all `Eq` or all `IsNotDistinctFrom`. The consumer needs to handle the reverse: receiving a Substrait plan that may have mixed keys (from other producers).

The Substrait spec actually has a different approach: each join key in Substrait can have its own comparison type. Let me check the Substrait proto definition more carefully.

Actually, looking at the Substrait spec, there's a `ComparisonJoinKey` which has a `simple_comparison_type` field that can be `Eq` or `IsNotDistinctFrom`. But the DataFusion consumer currently reads from the `expression` field of `JoinRel`, not from the comparison join keys.

Wait, let me check if there's another code path that handles comparison join keys

2026-06-01 04:53:29,637 - INFO - swea-agent-apache__datafusion-21121 - 💭 THOUGHT
No mixed join test file exists yet. The PR description says it's from a PR that hasn't been merged yet. The test file `mixed_join_equal_and_indistinct.json` would be added as part of the PR.

Now, let me reconsider my approach. The core issue is: the `nulls_equal_nulls` variable gets overwritten, so only the last condition's semantics are used.

Actually, wait. Let me re-read the original code more carefully:

```rust
nulls_equal_nulls = match x.op {
    Operator::Eq => false,
    Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom => true,
    _ => unreachable!(),
};
```

This sets `nulls_equal_nulls` for EVERY key, overwriting the previous value. So if you have:
- `t1.id = t2.id` → `nulls_equal_nulls = false`
- `t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val` → `nulls_equal_nulls = true`

The final value is `true` (from the last key), meaning ALL keys are treated as `NullEqualsNull`. This means `t1.id = t2.id` would be treated as `IS NOT DISTINCT FROM`, which is incorrect.

If the order is reversed:
- `t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val` → `nulls_equal_nulls = true`
- `t1.id = t2.id` → `nulls_equal_nulls = false`

The final value is `false`, meaning ALL keys are treated as `NullEqualsNothing`. This means `t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val` would be treated as regular `=`, which is also incorrect.

So the bug is clear: when mixed, one of the semantics is applied to all keys, which is wrong.

Now, what's the correct fix? Let me look at how the physical plan handles the filter for joins. The key question: for outer joins, is the filter applied as part of the join condition (before null-padding) or after?

   312	    let (build_indices, probe_indices) = equal_rows_arr(
   313	        &build_indices_unfiltered,
   314	        &probe_indices_unfiltered,
   315	        build_side_values,
   316	        probe_side_values,
   317	        null_equality,
   318	    )?;
   319	
   320	    // Reclaim buffers
   321	    *build_indices_buffer = build_indices_unfiltered.into_parts().1.into();
   322	    *probe_indices_buffer = probe_indices_unfiltered.into_parts().1.into();
   323	
   324	    Ok((build_indices, probe_indices, next_offset))
   325	}
   326	
   327	/// Counts the number of distinct elements in the input array.
   328	///
   329	/// The input array must be sorted (e.g., `[0, 1, 1, 2, 2, ...]`) and contain no null values.
   330	#[inline]
   331	fn count_distinct_sorted_indices(indices: &UInt32Array) -> usize {
   332	    if indices.is_empty() {
   333	        return 0;
   334	    }
   335	
   336	    debug_assert!(indices.null_count() == 0);
   337	
   338	    let values_buf = indices.values();
   339	    let values = values_buf.as_ref();
   340	    let mut iter = values.iter();
   341	    let Some(&first) = iter.next() else {
   342	        return 0;
   343	    };
   344	
   345	    let mut count = 1usize;
   346	    let mut last = first;
   347	    for &value in iter {
   348	        if value != last {
   349	            last = value;
   350	            count += 1;
   351	        }
   352	    }
   353	    count
   354	}
   355

   915	pub(crate) fn apply_join_filter_to_indices(
   916	    build_input_buffer: &RecordBatch,
   917	    probe_batch: &RecordBatch,
   918	    build_indices: UInt64Array,
   919	    probe_indices: UInt32Array,
   920	    filter: &JoinFilter,
   921	    build_side: JoinSide,
   922	    max_intermediate_size: Option<usize>,
   923	    join_type: JoinType,
   924	) -> Result<(UInt64Array, UInt32Array)> {
   925	    if build_indices.is_empty() && probe_indices.is_empty() {
   926	        return Ok((build_indices, probe_indices));
   927	    };
   928	
   929	    let filter_result = if let Some(max_size) = max_intermediate_size {
   930	        let mut filter_results =
   931	            Vec::with_capacity(build_indices.len().div_ceil(max_size));
   932	
   933	        for i in (0..build_indices.len()).step_by(max_size) {
   934	            let end = min(build_indices.len(), i + max_size);
   935	            let len = end - i;
   936	            let intermediate_batch = build_batch_from_indices(
   937	                filter.schema(),
   938	                build_input_buffer,
   939	                probe_batch,
   940	                &build_indices.slice(i, len),
   941	                &probe_indices.slice(i, len),
   942	                filter.column_indices(),
   943	                build_side,
   944	                join_type,
   945	            )?;
   946	            let filter_result = filter
   947	                .expression()
   948	                .evaluate(&intermediate_batch)?
   949	                .into_array(intermediate_batch.num_rows())?;
   950	            filter_results.push(filter_result);
   951	        }
   952	
   953	        let filter_refs: Vec<&dyn Array> =
   954	            filter_results.iter().map(|a| a.as_ref()).collect();
   955	
   956	        compute::concat(&filter_refs)?
   957	    } else {
   958	        let intermediate_batch = build_batch_from_indices(
   959	            filter.schema(),
   960	            build_input_buffer,
   961	            probe_batch,
   962	            &build_indices,
   963	            &probe_indices,
   964	            filter.column_indices(),
   965	            build_side,
   966	            join_type,
   967	        )?;
   968	
   969	        filter
   970	            .expression()
   971	            .evaluate(&intermediate_batch)?
   972	            .into_array(intermediate_batch.num_rows())?
   973	    };
   974	
   975	    let mask = as_boolean_array(&filter_result)?;
   976	
   977	    let left_filtered = compute::filter(&build_indices, mask)?;
   978	    let right_filtered = compute::filter(&probe_indices, mask)?;
   979	    Ok((
   980	        downcast_array(left_filtered.as_ref()),
   981	        downcast_array(right_filtered.as_ref()),
   982	    ))
   983	}
   984	
   985	/// Creates a [RecordBatch] with zero columns but the given row count.
   986	/// Used when a join has an empty projection (e.g. `SELECT count(1) ...`).
   987	fn new_empty_schema_batch(schema: &Schema, row_count: usize) -> Result<RecordBatch> {
   988	    let options = RecordBatchOptions::new().with_row_count(Some(row_count));
   989	    Ok(RecordBatch::try_new_with_options(
   990	        Arc::new(schema.clone()),
   991	        vec![],
   992	        &options,
   993	    )?)
   994	}
