  1109	pub(crate) fn adjust_indices_by_join_type(
  1110	    left_indices: UInt64Array,
  1111	    right_indices: UInt32Array,
  1112	    adjust_range: Range<usize>,
  1113	    join_type: JoinType,
  1114	    preserve_order_for_right: bool,
  1115	) -> Result<(UInt64Array, UInt32Array)> {
  1116	    match join_type {
  1117	        JoinType::Inner => {
  1118	            // matched
  1119	            Ok((left_indices, right_indices))
  1120	        }
  1121	        JoinType::Left => {
  1122	            // matched
  1123	            Ok((left_indices, right_indices))
  1124	            // unmatched left row will be produced in the end of loop, and it has been set in the left visited bitmap
  1125	        }
  1126	        JoinType::Right => {
  1127	            // combine the matched and unmatched right result together
  1128	            append_right_indices(
  1129	                left_indices,
  1130	                right_indices,
  1131	                adjust_range,
  1132	                preserve_order_for_right,
  1133	            )
  1134	        }
  1135	        JoinType::Full => {
  1136	            append_right_indices(left_indices, right_indices, adjust_range, false)
  1137	        }
  1138	        JoinType::RightSemi => {
  1139	            // need to remove the duplicated record in the right side
  1140	            let right_indices = get_semi_indices(adjust_range, &right_indices);
  1141	            // the left_indices will not be used later for the `right semi` join
  1142	            Ok((left_indices, right_indices))
  1143	        }
  1144	        JoinType::RightAnti => {
  1145	            // need to remove the duplicated record in the right side
  1146	            // get the anti index for the right side
  1147	            let right_indices = get_anti_indices(adjust_range, &right_indices);
  1148	            // the left_indices will not be used later for the `right anti` join
  1149	            Ok((left_indices, right_indices))
  1150	        }
  1151	        JoinType::RightMark => {
  1152	            let right_indices = get_mark_indices(&adjust_range, &right_indices);
  1153	            let left_indices_vec: Vec<u64> = adjust_range.map(|i| i as u64).collect();
  1154	            let left_indices = UInt64Array::from(left_indices_vec);
  1155	            Ok((left_indices, right_indices))
  1156	        }
  1157	        JoinType::LeftSemi | JoinType::LeftAnti | JoinType::LeftMark => {
  1158	            // matched or unmatched left row will be produced in the end of loop
  1159	            // When visit the right batch, we can output the matched left row and don't need to wait the end of loop
  1160	            Ok((
  1161	                UInt64Array::from_iter_values(vec![]),
  1162	                UInt32Array::from_iter_values(vec![]),
  1163	            ))
  1164	        }
  1165	    }
  1166	}
  1167	
  1168	/// Appends right indices to left indices based on the specified order mode.
  1169	///
  1170	/// The function operates in two modes:
  1171	/// 1. If `preserve_order_for_right` is true, probe matched and unmatched indices
  1172	///    are inserted in order using the `append_probe_indices_in_order()` method.
  1173	/// 2. Otherwise, unmatched probe indices are simply appended after matched ones.
  1174	///
  1175	/// # Parameters
  1176	/// - `left_indices`: UInt64Array of left indices.
  1177	/// - `right_indices`: UInt32Array of right indices.
  1178	/// - `adjust_range`: Range to adjust the right indices.
  1179	/// - `preserve_order_for_right`: Boolean flag to determine the mode of operation.
  1180	///
  1181	/// # Returns
  1182	/// A tuple of updated `UInt64Array` and `UInt32Array`.
  1183	pub(crate) fn append_right_indices(
  1184	    left_indices: UInt64Array,
  1185	    right_indices: UInt32Array,
  1186	    adjust_range: Range<usize>,
  1187	    preserve_order_for_right: bool,
  1188	) -> Result<(UInt64Array, UInt32Array)> {
  1189	    if preserve_order_for_right {
  1190	        Ok(append_probe_indices_in_order(
  1191	            &left_indices,
  1192	            &right_indices,
  1193	            adjust_range,
  1194	        ))
  1195	    } else {
  1196	        let right_unmatched_indices = get_anti_indices(adjust_range, &right_indices);
  1197	
  1198	        if right_unmatched_indices.is_empty() {
  1199	            Ok((left_indices, right_indices))
  1200	        } else {
  1201	            // `into_builder()` can fail here when there is nothing to be filtered and
  1202	            // left_indices or right_indices has the same reference to the cached indices.
  1203	            // In that case, we use a slower alternative.
  1204	
  1205	            // the new left indices: left_indices + null array
  1206	            let mut new_left_indices_builder =
  1207	                left_indices.into_builder().unwrap_or_else(|left_indices| {
  1208	                    let mut builder = UInt64Builder::with_capacity(
  1209	                        left_indices.len() + right_unmatched_indices.len(),
  1210	                    );

I can see that for Left/Full outer joins, the `adjust_indices_by_join_type` adds unmatched rows AFTER the filter is applied. So the filter is applied to matched rows, and then unmatched rows from the outer side are added. This means the filter IS part of the join condition, not a post-join filter.

So for a LEFT JOIN with filter `t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val`:
1. Hash join matches on equijoin keys
2. Filter is applied to matched pairs
3. Unmatched left rows are added with NULLs for right columns

This means moving `IsNotDistinctFrom` to the filter when mixed with `Eq` keys is semantically CORRECT for outer joins too! The filter is applied as part of the join, not after.

Wait, but there's a subtlety: when a left row has no match on the equijoin keys, it's output with NULLs for right columns. The filter `t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.val` would evaluate to `t1.val IS NOT DISTINCT FROM NULL` which is FALSE (assuming t1.val is not null). So the left row would still be in the output because it's unmatched - the filter is only applied to matched pairs.

Actually, let me verify this by looking at the hash join stream code more carefully:

So both approaches should give the same result for matched rows.

All tests pass. Now I'm fairly confident in my fix, but let me also think about whether there's a simpler/better approach.

Actually, looking at the extract_equijoin_predicate optimizer rule again:

```rust
// Only convert when there are NO equijoin predicates, to be conservative.
if on.is_empty()
    && equijoin_predicates.is_empty()
    && non_equijoin_expr.is_some()
{
    let (equijoin_predicates, non_equijoin_expr) =
        split_is_not_distinct_from_and_other_join_predicate(...);
    if !equijoin_predicates.is_empty() {
        on.extend(equijoin_predicates);
        return Ok(Transformed::yes(LogicalPlan::Join(Join {
            ...
            null_equality: NullEquality::NullEqualsNull,
        })));
    }
}
```

This optimizer only converts `IsNotDistinctFrom` to join keys when there are NO existing equijoin predicates AND no existing join keys. So it never creates a mixed situation. It only converts when all keys are `IsNotDistinctFrom`.

My consumer fix aligns with this: when mixed, keep `Eq` as join keys and `IsNotDistinctFrom` in filter. When all are `IsNotDistinctFrom`, use `NullEqualsNull`.

But wait, there's another subtlety. The optimizer checks `on.is_empty()` - meaning if there are already join keys set (from the SQL parser), it won't convert `IsNotDistinctFrom` to join keys. But the substrait consumer starts with empty `on` and populates it from the expression. So the consumer is the one creating the join keys initially.

My fix is consistent: if only `IsNotDistinctFrom` keys exist, use `NullEqualsNull`. If mixed, keep `Eq` as keys and move `IsNotDistinctFrom` to filter. This matches the optimizer's conservative approach.

Let me also think about an alternative: instead of moving `IsNotDistinctFrom` to filter when mixed, we could move `Eq` to filter and use `NullEqualsNull` for all. But that would be wrong for outer joins because `Eq` in filter would be applied to matched pairs only, which is the same as `IsNotDistinctFrom` in filter. Actually both approaches work for outer joins because the filter is applied during join.

Hmm, but which is better? With `NullEqualsNull`:
- All keys are treated as `IS NOT DISTINCT FROM`
- `Eq` keys would match null=null, which is incorrect for `=` semantics

With `NullEqualsNothing` (my approach):
- `Eq` keys are treated as `=`
- `IsNotDistinctFrom` in filter handles null=null correctly

My approach is better because it correctly handles the `Eq` semantics and the `IsNotDistinctFrom` semantics via the filter.

Now, one more thought: what if we have `IsNotDistinctFrom` with expression arguments (not simple columns)? In the all-`IsNotDistinctFrom` case, these go to filter (since they're not column pairs). Then we'd have `NullEqualsNull` for the column-pair join keys, and the expression `IsNotDistinctFrom` in filter. That's correct.

What about the mixed case with expression `Eq`? E.g., `t1.a + 1 = t2.b AND t1.c IS NOT DISTINCT FROM t2.d`. The `Eq` with expression goes to filter, the `IsNotDistinctFrom` goes to filter, and there are no join keys. In this case, `mixed_semantics` would be false (since there are no column-pair keys for either), so we'd have `nulls_equal_nulls = false` and empty join keys with both expressions in filter. That's correct.

OK, I'm satisfied with my fix. Let me also check if there are any other places in the codebase that might have the same issue.

Let me also check the `from_substrait_jointype` function to see if there's anything related to join type handling that could affect this...

    18	use crate::logical_plan::consumer::SubstraitConsumer;
    19	use datafusion::common::{Column, JoinType, NullEquality, not_impl_err, plan_err};
    20	use datafusion::logical_expr::requalify_sides_if_needed;
    21	use datafusion::logical_expr::utils::split_conjunction;
    22	use datafusion::logical_expr::{
    23	    BinaryExpr, Expr, LogicalPlan, LogicalPlanBuilder, Operator,
    24	};
    25	
    26	use substrait::proto::{JoinRel, join_rel};
    27	
    28	pub async fn from_join_rel(
    29	    consumer: &impl SubstraitConsumer,
    30	    join: &JoinRel,
    31	) -> datafusion::common::Result<LogicalPlan> {
    32	    if join.post_join_filter.is_some() {
    33	        return not_impl_err!("JoinRel with post_join_filter is not yet supported");
    34	    }
    35	
    36	    let left: LogicalPlanBuilder = LogicalPlanBuilder::from(
    37	        consumer.consume_rel(join.left.as_ref().unwrap()).await?,
    38	    );
    39	    let right = LogicalPlanBuilder::from(
    40	        consumer.consume_rel(join.right.as_ref().unwrap()).await?,
    41	    );
    42	    let (left, right, _requalified) = requalify_sides_if_needed(left, right)?;
    43	
    44	    let join_type = from_substrait_jointype(join.r#type)?;
    45	    // The join condition expression needs full input schema and not the output schema from join since we lose columns from
    46	    // certain join types such as semi and anti joins
    47	    let in_join_schema = left.schema().join(right.schema())?;
    48	
    49	    // If join expression exists, parse the `on` condition expression, build join and return
    50	    // Otherwise, build join with only the filter, without join keys
    51	    match &join.expression.as_ref() {
    52	        Some(expr) => {
    53	            let on = consumer.consume_expression(expr, &in_join_schema).await?;
    54	            // The join expression can contain both equal and non-equal ops.
    55	            // As of datafusion 31.0.0, the equal and non equal join conditions are in separate fields.
    56	            // So we extract each part as follows:
    57	            // - If an Eq or IsNotDistinctFrom op is encountered, add the left column, right column and is_null_equal_nulls to `join_ons` vector
    58	            // - Otherwise we add the expression to join_filter (use conjunction if filter already exists)
    59	            let (join_ons, nulls_equal_nulls, join_filter) =
    60	                split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality(&on);
    61	            let (left_cols, right_cols): (Vec<_>, Vec<_>) =
    62	                itertools::multiunzip(join_ons);
    63	            let null_equality = if nulls_equal_nulls {
    64	                NullEquality::NullEqualsNull
    65	            } else {
    66	                NullEquality::NullEqualsNothing
    67	            };
    68	            left.join_detailed(
    69	                right.build()?,
    70	                join_type,
    71	                (left_cols, right_cols),
    72	                join_filter,
    73	                null_equality,
    74	            )?
    75	            .build()
    76	        }
    77	        None => {
    78	            let on: Vec<String> = vec![];
    79	            left.join_detailed(
    80	                right.build()?,
    81	                join_type,
    82	                (on.clone(), on),
    83	                None,
    84	                NullEquality::NullEqualsNothing,
    85	            )?
    86	            .build()
    87	        }
    88	    }
    89	}
    90	
    91	fn split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality(
    92	    filter: &Expr,
    93	) -> (Vec<(Column, Column)>, bool, Option<Expr>) {
    94	    let exprs = split_conjunction(filter);
    95	
    96	    // Track whether we have seen Eq (null equals nothing) and IsNotDistinctFrom (null equals null) keys
    97	    let mut has_eq_keys = false;
    98	    let mut has_null_eq_null_keys = false;
    99	
   100	    // First pass: detect if we have mixed null semantics
   101	    for expr in &exprs {
   102	        if let Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) = expr {
   103	            match binary_expr {
   104	                BinaryExpr {
   105	                    op: Operator::Eq, ..
   106	                } => has_eq_keys = true,
   107	                BinaryExpr {
   108	                    op: Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
   109	                    ..
   110	                } => has_null_eq_null_keys = true,
   111	                _ => {}
   112	            }
   113	        }
   114	    }
   115	
   116	    // If we have mixed null semantics (both Eq and IsNotDistinctFrom keys),
   117	    // we cannot represent this with a single null_equality per join.
   118	    // In this case, we keep the Eq keys as join keys with NullEqualsNothing
   119	    // and move the IsNotDistinctFrom keys to the filter to preserve their
   120	    // null-equal semantics.
   121	    let mixed_semantics = has_eq_keys && has_null_eq_null_keys;
   122	
   123	    let mut accum_join_keys: Vec<(Column, Column)> = vec![];
   124	    let mut accum_filters: Vec<Expr> = vec![];
   125	
   126	    for expr in exprs {
   127	        match expr {
   128	            Expr::BinaryExpr(binary_expr) => match binary_expr {
   129	                BinaryExpr {
   130	                    left,
   131	                    op: Operator::Eq,
   132	                    right,
   133	                } => {
   134	                    match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
   135	                        (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
   136	                            accum_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
   137	                        }
   138	                        _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   139	                    }
   140	                }
   141	                BinaryExpr {
   142	                    left,
   143	                    op: Operator::IsNotDistinctFrom,
   144	                    right,
   145	                } => {
   146	                    if mixed_semantics {
   147	                        // Move IsNotDistinctFrom expressions to filter
   148	                        accum_filters.push(expr.clone());
   149	                    } else {
   150	                        match (left.as_ref(), right.as_ref()) {
   151	                            (Expr::Column(l), Expr::Column(r)) => {
   152	                                accum_join_keys.push((l.clone(), r.clone()));
   153	                            }
   154	                            _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   155	                        }
   156	                    }
   157	                }
   158	                _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   159	            },
   160	            _ => accum_filters.push(expr.clone()),
   161	        }
   162	    }
   163	
   164	    let nulls_equal_nulls = !mixed_semantics && has_null_eq_null_keys;
   165	    let join_filter = accum_filters.into_iter().reduce(Expr::and);
   166	    (accum_join_keys, nulls_equal_nulls, join_filter)
   167	}
   168	
   169	fn from_substrait_jointype(join_type: i32) -> datafusion::common::Result<JoinType> {
   170	    if let Ok(substrait_join_type) = join_rel::JoinType::try_from(join_type) {
   171	        match substrait_join_type {
   172	            join_rel::JoinType::Inner => Ok(JoinType::Inner),
   173	            join_rel::JoinType::Left => Ok(JoinType::Left),
   174	            join_rel::JoinType::Right => Ok(JoinType::Right),
   175	            join_rel::JoinType::Outer => Ok(JoinType::Full),
   176	            join_rel::JoinType::LeftAnti => Ok(JoinType::LeftAnti),
   177	            join_rel::JoinType::LeftSemi => Ok(JoinType::LeftSemi),
   178	            join_rel::JoinType::LeftMark => Ok(JoinType::LeftMark),
   179	            join_rel::JoinType::RightMark => Ok(JoinType::RightMark),
   180	            join_rel::JoinType::RightAnti => Ok(JoinType::RightAnti),
   181	            join_rel::JoinType::RightSemi => Ok(JoinType::RightSemi),
   182	            _ => plan_err!("unsupported join type {substrait_join_type:?}"),
   183	        }
   184	    } else {
   185	        plan_err!("invalid join type variant {join_type}")
   186	    }
   187	}
   188

Let me now summarize the changes:\n\n## Summary\n\nThe bug was in the `split_eq_and_noneq_join_predicate_with_nulls_equality` function in `/testbed/datafusion/substrait/src/logical_plan/consumer/rel/join_rel.rs`.\n\n### Problem\nThe function processes join conditions (a conjunction of expressions) and splits them into:\n- Join keys (for `Eq` and `IsNotDistinctFrom` operators with column arguments)\n- Filter expressions (everything else)\n- A single `null_equality` flag indicating whether nulls should be treated as equal\n\nThe bug was that the `nulls_equal_nulls` variable was overwritten on each iteration of the loop, so only the **last** join condition's null semantics were preserved.
